<Rate>1<//Rate><Text>Goodwill is one of the greatest disappointments in modern America. Arrogance is the motto of this so-called ‚Äúcharitable organization‚Äù. In fact, contrary to popular belief, maybe it isn‚Äôt a charitable organization at all. Maybe those running it have some other motivation for being in business. I muse about this because on a few occasions over several years, as the circumstance would arise, our family has tried to donate recyclable, perfectly usable clothes, shoes, brick-a-brack, electronics, toys and other household items. The facilities tend to be convenient to get to but, inevitably, we would have to take our good intentions elsewhere. Staff constantly refuses virtually everything we offer. If this were an occasional occurrence relative to the odd unusable or otherwise not salable/recyclable/acceptable item it would be understandable but it has, instead, been a consistent occurrence over a long period of time. Clearly they prefer that Joe or Jane Public not darken the Goodwill door with their silly philanthropic notions. No doubt the management curmudgeons running this operation would spit out some bureaucratic non-response to this criticism, were they inclined,  but the fact remains that the average person will NOT be able to easily donate their used items here. It‚Äôs baffling, and frustrating, because the things we wish to give seem as good or better than what is on display in the store. Go figure. Make your donations, help your neighbors some other way. You‚Äôre likely to waste your time coming here. As a Los Angeles area organization meant primarily to serve the less privileged, or more thrifty, Out-of-the-Closet is much more responsible and well attuned to the needs of the community than these Goodwill people and other local shops will be far more welcoming.</Text>< userid>

<review>Delicious food! It seems Peruvian inspired with a Mexican influence and a northern California cuisine drive.     I've passed by but finally stopped in.   A great little place we need so bad in this neighborhood! Thank you!

The huevos rancheros are a nice twist on the classic. Less salsa than normal, each egg in its own tortilla almost like a taco.  Underneath the egg is a bed of black beans and cheese.  Sour cream in top.  Sliced avacado and watermelon garnish the plate.  And the passion fruit agua fresca is delish.

The service could have been warmer and friendlier, instead I felt I was bothering the  young lady who served me. Or she was really shy.  Either way, the ambience and food will have me back here soon and often!!!< /review>< pics>

< Review>
This is a beautiful theater, not too big. The only complaint I have is that USC needs to put more signage up to tell you where to go from the prospective parking situation you've gotten yourself into. I asked 2 students in passing where Bovard was and neither knew, so I switched it up and asked where the Tommy Trojan statue was and that was the key. I had been told in an email that the theater was by that statue- thank goodness for that tidbit of info.</Review>

<user_id>106755311109474150935</user_id><Time>1447834919072</Time><review>Bovard gave me a sour impression to start. At orientation they crammed all the incoming freshman in here to deliver "this school is awesome" indoctrination - you know, those endless speeches by over-excited alumni-administrators who don't know when to stop talking and don't pay attention to the distracted faces in the crowd.

There was better fare with time. Famous people come here to speak all the time, and the experience is as good as they make it.

The interior feels dark and dingy. The brick exterior is beautiful, and it's actually genuine, unlike many of the newer additions to campus. It feels lived-in, like people have actually spent time here and done interesting things in this building.<//review>< Name>

< user_name>
Pamela Tu<//user_name>
< pics>
None</pics>
<text>I have been here twice for a Vision and Voice performance (Santa Fe Aspen Ballet and Ballet Memphis). Ticket assignments are first come first serve so try to come at least an hour early to snag the orchestra seats. Otherwise you'll be stuck with the balcony seats. Bovard Auditorium is small enough that almost any section should be fine but I enjoy being close to the stage. Sometimes the line is shorter if you are on the non-affiliated list (versus the staff, alumni, students list). For example, today the affiliated line was much longer because they were giving out free t-shirts. I decided to forgo the free t-shirts for a shorter line. Priorities! Take the Metro, take a gamble parking in the residential area or pay $10 to park in the structure.</text>< resp>

<Rate>4</Rate><Text>This is a fantastic store for throwaway items. Seasonal little accents and accessories, stuff for kids, stuff for single use. You name it, they got it.

Obviously, unless you have serious financial constraints and you need an item NOW, this isn't the place to shop for long lasting, high quality things. However, they come in really handy when you're in a bind. I needed a strainer, bought it here for a buck, used it that day, washed it, and it was rusted within a few days.

This place shines for one-time use, disposable, or seasonal items. I've bought a boat-load of seasonal accents and party supplies here, and saved a ton of money doing it.

The only reason for the 4 stars instead of 5 is that every time I go in, the store is a complete mess, especially in the front, where they have carts full of returns piled up.</Text><username>Peter B< /username>< userid>
